## Section 001: Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed title does not yet define how a capability set should become a minimal plugin layout and manifest whose components are discoverable, portable, nonduplicated, versioned, and testable after packaging
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because discovery depends on exact package topology and parsed configuration, while portability and maintenance depend on avoiding cwd assumptions, duplicate registrations, unnecessary custom paths, and undocumented component ownership
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: components are nested under the manifest directory, custom paths duplicate defaults, absolute or parent paths leak local layout, names collide, manifest claims exceed packaged files, or archived field behavior is assumed current
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this reference for Claude Code plugin package structure and manifest decisions, not as current authoritative schema for unrelated extension ecosystems
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add a capability-to-component matrix, minimal-manifest rule, path and duplication invariants, package lifecycle tests, conflict handling, scale alternatives, and archived-versus-current evidence labels
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the manifest is a capability index and trust boundary, not a directory catalog; every declaration expands what the host loads, starts, or exposes
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to place the manifest at `.claude-plugin/plugin.json`, keep components at plugin root in conventional directories, create only used component types, rely on defaults, use relative manifest paths and plugin-root runtime references, and validate a packaged clean install
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because discovery depends on exact package topology and parsed configuration, while portability and maintenance depend on avoiding cwd assumptions, duplicate registrations, unnecessary custom paths, and undocumented component ownership
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; components are nested under the manifest directory, custom paths duplicate defaults, absolute or parent paths leak local layout, names collide, manifest claims exceed packaged files, or archived field behavior is assumed current
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: use this reference for Claude Code plugin package structure and manifest decisions, not as current authoritative schema for unrelated extension ecosystems
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add a capability-to-component matrix, minimal-manifest rule, path and duplication invariants, package lifecycle tests, conflict handling, scale alternatives, and archived-versus-current evidence labels
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies the manifest is a capability index and trust boundary, not a directory catalog; every declaration expands what the host loads, starts, or exposes
### Question 03: When does the default work well?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the default works well under these conditions: the plugin has one coherent purpose, conventional component boundaries fit, names are unique, every declared path exists, internal references survive relocation, and clean-install discovery can be observed
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: those conditions support the recommendation because discovery depends on exact package topology and parsed configuration, while portability and maintenance depend on avoiding cwd assumptions, duplicate registrations, unnecessary custom paths, and undocumented component ownership
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the success case ends where components are nested under the manifest directory, custom paths duplicate defaults, absolute or parent paths leak local layout, names collide, manifest claims exceed packaged files, or archived field behavior is assumed current
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: treat these operating conditions as bounded by use this reference for Claude Code plugin package structure and manifest decisions, not as current authoritative schema for unrelated extension ecosystems
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: add an explicit use-when statement grounded in the plugin has one coherent purpose, conventional component boundaries fit, names are unique, every declared path exists, internal references survive relocation, and clean-install discovery can be observed
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: show the second-order benefit that the manifest is a capability index and trust boundary, not a directory catalog; every declaration expands what the host loads, starts, or exposes
### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: components are nested under the manifest directory, custom paths duplicate defaults, absolute or parent paths leak local layout, names collide, manifest claims exceed packaged files, or archived field behavior is assumed current
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: the boundary is important because the main risks are valid JSON with invalid semantics, source-tree tests masking missing package files, plugin-root versus working-directory confusion, custom paths supplementing rather than replacing defaults, nested discovery assumptions, stale version metadata, and hidden component conflicts
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: crossing one boundary does not invalidate the default where the plugin has one coherent purpose, conventional component boundaries fit, names are unique, every declared path exists, internal references survive relocation, and clean-install discovery can be observed
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: distinguish a genuine failure from an out-of-scope case using use this reference for Claude Code plugin package structure and manifest decisions, not as current authoritative schema for unrelated extension ecosystems
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: prescribe this bounded recovery instead of forcing the default: remove unused fields, return to default directories, split independent capability domains into separate plugins, generate a combined hook file at build time, place deterministic shared logic in a library, or defer custom organization until scale requires it
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: retain uncertainty explicitly: the corpus is archived and current Claude Code manifest schema or discovery behavior was not refreshed, so release claims require tests against the installed version
### Question 05: Which alternatives and tradeoffs matter?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: the meaningful alternatives are these: remove unused fields, return to default directories, split independent capability domains into separate plugins, generate a combined hook file at build time, place deterministic shared logic in a library, or defer custom organization until scale requires it
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: compare those alternatives against the decision to determine how to choose a Claude Code plugin directory structure, manifest fields, component paths, names, and lifecycle checks for the plugin's actual capabilities and distribution scope
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: alternatives become option theater when valid JSON with invalid semantics, source-tree tests masking missing package files, plugin-root versus working-directory confusion, custom paths supplementing rather than replacing defaults, nested discovery assumptions, stale version metadata, and hidden component conflicts
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: compare only choices allowed by use this reference for Claude Code plugin package structure and manifest decisions, not as current authoritative schema for unrelated extension ecosystems
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: revise the guidance to contrast the default with each viable recovery and apply this section-specific change: add a capability-to-component matrix, minimal-manifest rule, path and duplication invariants, package lifecycle tests, conflict handling, scale alternatives, and archived-versus-current evidence labels
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: make the tradeoff consequential by connecting it to the manifest is a capability index and trust boundary, not a directory catalog; every declaration expands what the host loads, starts, or exposes
### Question 06: Which gotchas and failure modes matter most?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 06 on gotchas and failure modes: the highest-value warnings are valid JSON with invalid semantics, source-tree tests masking missing package files, plugin-root versus working-directory confusion, custom paths supplementing rather than replacing defaults, nested discovery assumptions, stale version metadata, and hidden component conflicts

- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 06 on gotchas and failure modes: evaluate each warning inside this assumption set: use this reference for Claude Code plugin package structure and manifest decisions, not as current authoritative schema for unrelated extension ecosystems
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 06 on gotchas and failure modes: add observable warning signs plus the recovery path remove unused fields, return to default directories, split independent capability domains into separate plugins, generate a combined hook file at build time, place deterministic shared logic in a library, or defer custom organization until scale requires it
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 06 on gotchas and failure modes: explain the systemic effect that the manifest is a capability index and trust boundary, not a directory catalog; every declaration expands what the host loads, starts, or exposes
### Question 07: What do good, bad, and borderline examples look like?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 07 on good, bad, and borderline examples: the operational comparison is Good: a skill-only plugin has one manifest and one `skills/<name>/SKILL.md`. Bad: all components live inside `.claude-plugin/` with local absolute paths. Borderline: categorized commands need custom paths only when each directory is packaged, conflict-tested, and documented
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 07 on good, bad, and borderline examples: the good case is credible because the plugin has one coherent purpose, conventional component boundaries fit, names are unique, every declared path exists, internal references survive relocation, and clean-install discovery can be observed

- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 07 on good, bad, and borderline examples: interpret all three examples within use this reference for Claude Code plugin package structure and manifest decisions, not as current authoritative schema for unrelated extension ecosystems
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 07 on good, bad, and borderline examples: revise the examples so each reveals a decision, consequence, and recovery while implementing this section-specific change: add a capability-to-component matrix, minimal-manifest rule, path and duplication invariants, package lifecycle tests, conflict handling, scale alternatives, and archived-versus-current evidence labels

- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Plugin Structure Manifest Patterns", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the resulting operational insight is to change course when the default is unsafe or insufficient, using these bounded alternatives: remove unused fields, return to default directories, split independent capability domains into separate plugins, generate a combined hook file at build time, place deterministic shared logic in a library, or defer custom organization until scale requires it This changes how the section resolves how to choose a Claude Code plugin directory structure, manifest fields, component paths, names, and lifecycle checks for the plugin's actual capabilities and distribution scope.

## Section 002: Source Evidence Mapping Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed presents six local paths that are three byte-identical archive and live-path pairs, plus three MCP rows that describe an adjacent integration model rather than native plugin manifest discovery
- **supporting_reason:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because copied files do not corroborate each other, and protocol-server documentation cannot establish native plugin manifest fields, path resolution, or discovery behavior
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: six paths become six votes, manifest examples are assumed current, MCP repositories define native package layout, or a source title substitutes for checking the relevant field and caveat
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply this source model to the frozen nine rows and maintain installed tests as a separate evidence class
- **revision_decision:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add duplicate lineage, claim-relative authority, MCP adjacency limits, current-version handoff, conflict treatment, and a provenance ledger while retaining every row
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that lineage-aware mapping reduces both context and false certainty, leaving more review attention for the real difference between declared package shape and observed loading

## Section 004: Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed recommends local-first evidence and verification but does not state that plugin structure should follow capabilities and lifecycle, with the manifest kept minimal and observed package behavior outranking assumed discovery
- **supporting_reason:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because convention reduces configuration and duplicate loading, while package-level tests expose missing files, path assumptions, name conflicts, and lifecycle effects that source-tree review cannot
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the manifest becomes an aspirational catalog, nested folders are assumed discoverable, custom paths accumulate without conflict checks, or structural neatness is valued over actual host loading

- **supporting_reason:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 10 on second-order deductions: that deduction follows from convention reduces configuration and duplicate loading, while package-level tests expose missing files, path assumptions, name conflicts, and lifecycle effects that source-tree review cannot
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 10 on second-order deductions: its reach is limited where the manifest becomes an aspirational catalog, nested folders are assumed discoverable, custom paths accumulate without conflict checks, or structural neatness is valued over actual host loading
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 10 on second-order deductions: carry the deduction forward only within apply the thesis to Claude Code plugin packages and keep MCP protocol claims or current host schema in their own evidence lanes
- **revision_decision:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 10 on second-order deductions: change the guidance by applying this concrete revision: replace generic synthesis with capability derivation, minimal declaration, package-truth testing, lifecycle evidence, scale alternatives, and freshness limits
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the resulting operational insight is to change course when the default is unsafe or insufficient, using these bounded alternatives: simplify to one component type, use build-time generation for complex hook configuration, split independent plugin domains, externalize shared code to `lib`, or postpone marketplace metadata This changes how the section resolves what governing rule should control plugin topology and manifest evolution from first capability through distribution.

## Section 007: Anti Pattern Registry Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed lists generic source and verification failures but omits plugin defects such as misplaced manifests, components under `.claude-plugin`, duplicate default and custom discovery, local paths, missing package files, collisions, and aspirational declarations

## Section 008: Verification Gate Command Set
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed supplies only a generated-reference verifier, while plugin acceptance also needs JSON parsing, current schema validation, package inventory, path checks, conflict detection, clean installation, component activation, update, disable, and removal evidence
- **supporting_reason:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because reference integrity cannot prove a package, and source-tree linting cannot prove discovery, process startup, name conflicts, or cleanup after relocation
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: delimiter or grep checks replace JSON parsing, installation uses the source folder, only one component is invoked, custom paths are not collision-tested, or uninstall is assumed clean
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: keep reference QA, package QA, and component behavior QA as separate evidence layers
- **revision_decision:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add structured and semantic validation, package inventory, portability and secret scans, clean-host lifecycle matrix, evidence packet, and focused validator while retaining the seed command
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that verification should follow the loader's causal sequence: parse, resolve, discover, register, initialize, activate, deactivate, and remove

## Section 009: Agent Usage Decision Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?

## Section 010: User Journey Scenario
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed identifies a platform builder selecting an extension surface but does not trace plugin capabilities into a manifest, package tree, clean installation, component activation, update, diagnosis, disable, and removal
- **supporting_reason:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the sequence exposes wrong-surface and missing-package errors before distribution and gives every declared capability a traceable path to observable host behavior
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the plugin purpose is incoherent, component ownership is shared implicitly, the package cannot be isolated, required secrets are embedded, or lifecycle effects cannot be inventoried
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this scenario for plugin packaging and route each component's internal behavior to dedicated guidance
- **revision_decision:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace the generic role statement with a capability-to-package lifecycle, checkpoints, failure exits, evidence packet, and good, bad, and borderline package outcomes
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the package journey is a bidirectional trace: every capability must reach a component, and every packaged component must justify a capability

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed bases adopt, adapt, and avoid on source agreement but omits practical choices among default and custom paths, minimal and rich metadata, one plugin and split packages, inline and file configuration, or flat and categorized components
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because custom structure can improve ownership and discovery at scale but increases manifest surface, duplicate-registration risk, package testing, migration, and user support
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: agreement between archive and external links substitutes for package need, adaptation works around an invalid manifest, avoid offers no route, or a full-featured example drives premature scaffolding
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: decide per package and capability domain, not by applying one layout to every plugin in a marketplace
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to reframe the four seed options around defaults, custom paths, package splitting, inline configuration, metadata depth, lifecycle cost, and reversible alternatives
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that custom structure should purchase a specific property such as ownership or permission separation; aesthetics alone cannot repay the additional loader and migration contracts

## Section 013: Theme Specific Artifact
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed requests a manifest compatibility matrix with install validation and failure examples, but its three generic rows omit host versions, package inventory, fields, paths, components, discovery, activation, effects, update, and removal
- **supporting_reason:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because compatibility is a relation among one artifact, one host, one environment, and one claim; a manifest alone cannot establish that relation
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the matrix lists aspirational checkmarks, reuses one source-tree run across platforms, omits negative cases, treats parse success as activation, or ignores processes and state after removal
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: require the full matrix for distribution and allow a small single-environment record for explicitly local plugins
- **revision_decision:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to expand the three fields into an artifact-host matrix, inventory and lifecycle evidence, failure cells, migration and removal checks, and support-scope rules
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the matrix turns compatibility from a plugin adjective into a versioned evidence set that can shrink or expand without ambiguity
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to record package hash, plugin and host versions, platform, install method, manifest fields, default and custom paths, packaged files, expected components, discovery and activation results, dependencies, effects, diagnostics, update migration, disable, and removal

## Section 016: Completeness Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed checks role, options, hierarchy, artifact, examples, metrics, and routing but omits capability coverage, exact package inventory, manifest semantics, default and custom path conflicts, portability, component lifecycle, updates, and removal
- **supporting_reason:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a package may satisfy prose completeness while omitting a component, loading an unexpected one, failing after relocation, or leaving processes and state behind
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: checkmarks lack evidence, one successful install covers all components, source-tree presence proves package inclusion, or supported platform and version cells are left implicit
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply full gates to distributed plugins and document justified reductions for local single-purpose packages
- **revision_decision:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to extend seed categories with evidence pointers, package graph invariants, compatibility cells, component lifecycle, migration, and final clean-host replay
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that package completeness is bidirectional equality between intended capabilities and observed components: neither omissions nor extras are acceptable without explanation
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?

## Section 017: Adjacent Reference Routing
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed names command, hook, MCP, settings, manifest, plugin, structure, and development references but does not define the capability boundary or handoff evidence for each
- **supporting_reason:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because structure determines what loads, while component references determine what loaded capabilities do; mixing the two hides distinct schemas, permissions, and failure modes
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: routing follows a similar noun, component behavior remains undocumented because the manifest declares it, several adjacent references load at once, or returned guidance silently adds capabilities
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: route after package responsibility is clear and keep manifest ownership with the package maintainer
- **revision_decision:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace generic pointers with capability triggers, minimal handoff fields, lifecycle ownership, return criteria, and cross-component examples
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that a good handoff preserves the loader boundary: package evidence says the component exists, component evidence says whether its behavior is acceptable
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to stay here for package layout and manifest; route command, agent, skill, hook, MCP, settings, marketplace, script, testing, or security questions to the owner of that component or lifecycle
- **supporting_reason:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because structure determines what loads, while component references determine what loaded capabilities do; mixing the two hides distinct schemas, permissions, and failure modes
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; routing follows a similar noun, component behavior remains undocumented because the manifest declares it, several adjacent references load at once, or returned guidance silently adds capabilities
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: route after package responsibility is clear and keep manifest ownership with the package maintainer
- **revision_decision:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: replace generic pointers with capability triggers, minimal handoff fields, lifecycle ownership, return criteria, and cross-component examples
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies a good handoff preserves the loader boundary: package evidence says the component exists, component evidence says whether its behavior is acceptable
### Question 03: When does the default work well?

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed bounds work by one task, ten sources, three delegated subtasks, and an audit, but structure workload is driven by component and path graph size, initialization effects, owners, release coupling, and compatibility cells
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because every component path, startup action, platform, host version, and owner multiplies package states that must remain consistent through install, update, disable, and removal
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: one manifest aggregates unrelated plugins, custom roots proliferate, parallel owners edit the same declaration, compatibility combinations grow unbounded, or raw source count is treated as capacity
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this model for package architecture and review capacity, not component runtime throughput
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to retain seed capacity metadata but add loader graph, initialization, ownership, release, compatibility, and decomposition boundaries
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the binding workload is the number of loader and lifecycle contracts a reviewer can reconcile, not the number of Markdown files
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to keep one coherent capability domain per package, minimize custom discovery edges, assign one owner per manifest and component path, isolate initialization effects, and split independent release or permission domains
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because every component path, startup action, platform, host version, and owner multiplies package states that must remain consistent through install, update, disable, and removal
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; one manifest aggregates unrelated plugins, custom roots proliferate, parallel owners edit the same declaration, compatibility combinations grow unbounded, or raw source count is treated as capacity
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: use this model for package architecture and review capacity, not component runtime throughput
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: retain seed capacity metadata but add loader graph, initialization, ownership, release, compatibility, and decomposition boundaries
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies the binding workload is the number of loader and lifecycle contracts a reviewer can reconcile, not the number of Markdown files

## Section 019: Reliability Target
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed proposes full evidence labels, 18-of-20 routing, zero unsupported claims, and universal recovery paths but does not classify them or cover expected component equality, portability, startup containment, update migration, and removal
- **supporting_reason:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because package invariants are deterministic for one artifact, while compatibility across hosts and environments needs explicit cohorts and cannot be inferred from a single installation
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: 18 of 20 is advertised as compatibility, complete labels imply clean loading, expected components omit unexpected ones, or removal documentation substitutes for residue checks
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: treat seed values as proposed contracts or sampling goals, never observed host or plugin reliability
- **revision_decision:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to classify targets, add package-set equality and lifecycle containment, define compatibility cohorts, require denominators, and prohibit unsupported achieved-rate claims
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that reliable loading requires both absence of omissions and absence of surprises; unexpected activation can be more dangerous than a missing feature
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to enforce hard gates for valid artifact identity, manifest-package agreement, no unexpected or duplicate components, portable paths, declared initialization, recovery guidance, and unsupported-claim rejection; sample host and platform outcomes separately
- **supporting_reason:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because package invariants are deterministic for one artifact, while compatibility across hosts and environments needs explicit cohorts and cannot be inferred from a single installation
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; 18 of 20 is advertised as compatibility, complete labels imply clean loading, expected components omit unexpected ones, or removal documentation substitutes for residue checks
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: treat seed values as proposed contracts or sampling goals, never observed host or plugin reliability
- **revision_decision:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: classify targets, add package-set equality and lifecycle containment, define compatibility cohorts, require denominators, and prohibit unsupported achieved-rate claims
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies reliable loading requires both absence of omissions and absence of surprises; unexpected activation can be more dangerous than a missing feature
### Question 03: When does the default work well?

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?

## Section 020: Failure Mode Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed covers drift, generic advice, context loss, and fanout but omits manifest parse, semantic validation, package omission, path resolution, discovery, collision, initialization, activation, update, disable, and removal failures
- **supporting_reason:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because phase localization determines blast radius and recovery; a parser rejection should not be handled like a started server or a package update that changed state
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: all failures become bad paths, custom declarations mask missing package files, retries ignore started processes, or a fixed manifest is assumed to clean previous initialization effects
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this table for package and loading failures and route internal component failures to their own references
- **revision_decision:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to retain generic rows and add loader-phase taxonomy, component-set diffs, effect containment, migration, clean replay, and recurrence feedback
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that failure blast radius follows the loader timeline: errors after initialization demand effect cleanup even if a later manifest repair succeeds
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to classify failures across artifact build, manifest parse, field semantics, path resolution, package inventory, discovery, registration, initialization, activation, migration, deactivation, or removal
- **supporting_reason:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because phase localization determines blast radius and recovery; a parser rejection should not be handled like a started server or a package update that changed state

- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: use this table for package and loading failures and route internal component failures to their own references

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed limits retries and pauses on red gates but does not define artifact identity, discovery cache, component process state, installation idempotency, or safe cleanup between plugin load attempts
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because blind reinstallation can mix artifacts, duplicate registrations, restart servers, rerun hooks, or hide the first failure behind cached state
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the same package is repeatedly enabled, custom paths are added per attempt, processes survive uninstall, a new version number masks unchanged bytes, or concurrent owners test one profile
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply controls to plugin packaging and host loading; let components own their internal retry policies
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add package and attempt identity, cache and effect ledger, idempotency, fresh-profile fallback, concurrency ownership, semantic pass criteria, and cleanup escalation
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that backpressure preserves package-state identity; once artifact, cache, and effects are ambiguous, a fresh profile is cheaper than reasoning from contaminated evidence
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to retry only after classifying the phase, preserving the exact package or rebuilding with a new hash, clearing owned cache and effects deliberately, changing a relevant prerequisite, and proving replay is idempotent or cleanly compensated
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because blind reinstallation can mix artifacts, duplicate registrations, restart servers, rerun hooks, or hide the first failure behind cached state
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; the same package is repeatedly enabled, custom paths are added per attempt, processes survive uninstall, a new version number masks unchanged bytes, or concurrent owners test one profile
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: apply controls to plugin packaging and host loading; let components own their internal retry policies
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add package and attempt identity, cache and effect ledger, idempotency, fresh-profile fallback, concurrency ownership, semantic pass criteria, and cleanup escalation
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies backpressure preserves package-state identity; once artifact, cache, and effects are ambiguous, a fresh profile is cheaper than reasoning from contaminated evidence
### Question 03: When does the default work well?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the default works well under these conditions: attempt identity, package hash, host profile, cache state, process and file ledger, changed prerequisite, budget, owner, and semantic success criteria are recorded

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: the same package is repeatedly enabled, custom paths are added per attempt, processes survive uninstall, a new version number masks unchanged bytes, or concurrent owners test one profile
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: the boundary is important because the main risks are auto-start MCP servers, session-bound discovery, hooks firing during tests, state migrations, plugin-root temp files, platform locks, and user data that must not be deleted during cleanup
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: crossing one boundary does not invalidate the default where attempt identity, package hash, host profile, cache state, process and file ledger, changed prerequisite, budget, owner, and semantic success criteria are recorded

- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: retain uncertainty explicitly: safe attempt budgets and host cache controls vary by current product implementation
### Question 05: Which alternatives and tradeoffs matter?

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed records sources, proof, timing, tool calls, context, delegation, retries, and concise audits but omits package hash, manifest fields, resolved paths, expected and observed components, loader phase, processes, files, and privacy
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because correlation across artifact, loader phase, and effect state distinguishes malformed packages, stale caches, collisions, component failures, and incomplete cleanup
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: logs contain tokens, only successful components appear, package identity is missing, path errors lack resolution context, or raw debug output overwhelms the decision record
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: capture package lifecycle evidence and route component-specific data to its owner
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add artifact and attempt correlation, resolved path and component-set events, phase and effect tracking, secret redaction, privacy limits, and reconstruction tests
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the most useful structural telemetry is set-based: expected versus observed components reveals omissions and surprises with little sensitive content
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed requires tool and timeout budgets plus resumability, but it does not define build, install, discovery, initialization, activation, update, or removal stages or guard timing against incorrect component sets
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because latency without correctness can improve by silently skipping work, and one total duration hides whether custom paths, startup servers, hooks, or package size dominate
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: cold and warm loads mix, only successful installs remain, source-tree timing replaces package timing, removal ends before process checks, or file count is treated as causal proof
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: evaluate package loading and maintenance workflow, not internal component or external server throughput
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to define staged timing, component correctness gates, cold and warm states, matched packages, failure inclusion, low-sample alternatives, and uncertainty
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the right performance unit is a correct lifecycle transition, because structural optimization that changes the loaded capability set is a behavior change
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed stops at multiple systems, ownership, unbounded discovery, production traffic, parallel edits, context drift, and large codebases but not plugin families, shared loader paths, component fanout, or version coordination
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because as components and owners grow, path collisions, duplicated loading, shared state, release skew, and compatibility combinations exceed what one package review can reconcile
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: one manifest spans unrelated systems, nested pseudo-plugins hide multiple ownership domains, many plugins share mutable files, cross-plugin names collide, or family releases have no version choreography
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this statement for package architecture and release coordination, not production service capacity
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add plugin-family, shared-resource, startup-fanout, dependency, version, compatibility, migration, and decommission boundaries
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that scale failure begins when package identity no longer predicts ownership, lifecycle, or loaded capability set
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to split independent capability or permission domains, keep one manifest owner, version shared libraries explicitly, isolate startup components, namespace cross-plugin identifiers, and coordinate compatibility and migration across plugin families
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because as components and owners grow, path collisions, duplicated loading, shared state, release skew, and compatibility combinations exceed what one package review can reconcile
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; one manifest spans unrelated systems, nested pseudo-plugins hide multiple ownership domains, many plugins share mutable files, cross-plugin names collide, or family releases have no version choreography
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: use this statement for package architecture and release coordination, not production service capacity
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add plugin-family, shared-resource, startup-fanout, dependency, version, compatibility, migration, and decommission boundaries
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies scale failure begins when package identity no longer predicts ownership, lifecycle, or loaded capability set
### Question 03: When does the default work well?

- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: those conditions support the recommendation because as components and owners grow, path collisions, duplicated loading, shared state, release skew, and compatibility combinations exceed what one package review can reconcile
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the success case ends where one manifest spans unrelated systems, nested pseudo-plugins hide multiple ownership domains, many plugins share mutable files, cross-plugin names collide, or family releases have no version choreography

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?

## Section 026: Evidence Boundary Notes
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed defines local, external, and combined evidence but not duplicate lineage, package artifact facts, current host parsing, observed component sets, lifecycle fixtures, or provisional architecture judgments

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: labels decorate unsupported prose, archive examples become current schema, package presence proves discovery, one host proves portability, MCP sources prove native fields, or uncertainty does not alter support claims
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply these labels to this reference and downstream manifest matrices while preserving exact seed labels
- **revision_decision:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to extend the three-label note with lineage, artifact, host, fixture, set-difference, combination, conflict, and compositional-confidence rules
